     <p>The <b>University of California, San Diego</b> (also referred to as <b>UC San Diego</b> or <b>UCSD</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/La_Jolla" title="La Jolla">La Jolla</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The university occupies 2,141 acres (866&nbsp;ha) near the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> with the main campus resting on approximately 1,152 acres (466&nbsp;ha).<sup id="cite_ref-Area_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Area-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Established in 1960 near the pre-existing <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Institution_of_Oceanography" title="Scripps Institution of Oceanography">Scripps Institution of Oceanography</a>, UCSD is the seventh oldest of the 10 <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> campuses and offers over 200 undergraduate and graduate degree programs, enrolling about 22,700 undergraduate and 6,300 graduate students. UCSD is one of America's <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> universities, which recognizes top public research universities in the United States.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>UC San Diego is organized into six undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Residential_colleges" title="Residential colleges" class="mw-redirect">residential colleges</a>, five graduate schools, and two professional medical schools. The university operates four research institutes, including the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_for_Telecommunications_and_Information_Technology" title="California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology">California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Supercomputer_Center" title="San Diego Supercomputer Center">San Diego Supercomputer Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Institution_of_Oceanography" title="Scripps Institution of Oceanography">Scripps Institution of Oceanography</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UC_San_Diego_Health_System" title="UC San Diego Health System">UC San Diego Medical Center</a>, and is also affiliated with several regional research centers, such as the <a href="/wiki/Salk_Institute_for_Biological_Studies" title="Salk Institute for Biological Studies">Salk Institute</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sanford-Burnham_Medical_Research_Institute" title="Sanford-Burnham Medical Research Institute">Sanford-Burnham Medical Research Institute</a>, the Sanford Consortium for Regenerative Medicine, and the <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Research_Institute" title="Scripps Research Institute">Scripps Research Institute</a>. The university also houses two <a href="/wiki/Think_tanks" title="Think tanks" class="mw-redirect">think tanks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Institute_on_Global_Conflict_and_Cooperation" title="Institute on Global Conflict and Cooperation" class="mw-redirect">Institute on Global Conflict and Cooperation</a> and Center for Comparative Immigration Studies. UC San Diego faculty, researchers, and alumni have won twenty <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prizes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Nobel_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> eight <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medals of Science</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows_Program" title="MacArthur Fellows Program">MacArthur Fellowships</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prizes</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Awards_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Awards-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jacobs_staff_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacobs_staff-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, of the current faculty, 29 have been elected to the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Jacobs_staff_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jacobs_staff-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> 95 to the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a>, and 106 to the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Awards_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Awards-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC San Diego student-athletes compete in 23 intercollegiate sports as the <a href="/wiki/UC_San_Diego_Tritons" title="UC San Diego Tritons">Tritons</a> in <a href="/wiki/Division_II_(NCAA)" title="Division II (NCAA)">Division II</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>. As a member of the <a href="/wiki/California_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="California Collegiate Athletic Association">California Collegiate Athletic Association</a>, the Tritons have won 24 championships in sports including soccer, volleyball, golf, tennis, water polo, softball, swimming, and diving. The official colors of the university and its athletic teams are <a href="/wiki/Navy_blue" title="Navy blue">navy blue</a> and California <a href="/wiki/Gold_(color)" title="Gold (color)">gold</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>When the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a> originally authorized the San Diego campus in 1956, it was planned to be a graduate and research institution, providing instruction in the sciences, mathematics, and engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Local citizens supported the idea, voting the same year to transfer to the university 59 acres (24&nbsp;ha) of mesa land on the coast near the preexisting <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Institution_of_Oceanography" title="Scripps Institution of Oceanography">Scripps Institution of Oceanography</a>. The Regents requested an additional gift of 550 acres (220&nbsp;ha) of undeveloped mesa land northeast of Scripps, as well as 500 acres (200&nbsp;ha) on the former site of <a href="/wiki/Camp_Calvin_B._Matthews" title="Camp Calvin B. Matthews">Camp Matthews</a> from the federal government, but <a href="/wiki/Roger_Revelle" title="Roger Revelle">Roger Revelle</a>, then director of Scripps Institution and main advocate for establishing the new campus, jeopardized the site selection by exposing the La Jolla community's exclusive real estate business practices, which were antagonistic to minority racial and religious groups. This outraged local conservatives, as well as Regent <a href="/wiki/Edwin_W._Pauley" title="Edwin W. Pauley">Edwin W. Pauley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> UC President <a href="/wiki/Clark_Kerr" title="Clark Kerr">Clark Kerr</a> satisfied San Diego city donors by changing the proposed name from University of California, La Jolla, to University of California, San Diego.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The city voted in agreement to its part in 1958, and the UC approved construction of the new campus in 1960. Because of the clash with Pauley, Revelle was not made chancellor. <a href="/wiki/Herbert_York" title="Herbert York">Herbert York</a>, first director of <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Livermore_National_Laboratory" title="Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory">Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory</a>, was designated instead.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerr_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kerr-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> York planned the main campus according to the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Oxbridge" title="Oxbridge">Oxbridge</a>&quot; model, relying on many of Revelle's ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg/220px-Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg/330px-Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg/440px-Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Scripps_Institution_1967.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Scripps Institution of Oceanography, 1967
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UC San Diego was the first general campus of the University of California to be designed &quot;from the top down&quot; in terms of research emphasis. Local leaders disagreed on whether the new school should be a technical research institute or a more broadly based school that included undergraduates as well. <a href="/wiki/John_Jay_Hopkins" title="John Jay Hopkins">John Jay Hopkins</a> of <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics" title="General Dynamics">General Dynamics Corporation</a> pledged one million dollars for the former while the City Council offered free land for the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman1_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gribble_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gribble-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The original authorization for the San Diego campus given by the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">UC Regents</a> in 1956 approved a &quot;graduate program in science and technology&quot; that included undergraduate programs, a compromise that won both the support of General Dynamics and the city voters' approval.<sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman1_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Harold_Urey" title="Harold Urey">Harold Urey</a>, a physicist from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hans_Suess" title="Hans Suess">Hans Suess</a>, who had published the first paper on the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_effect" title="Greenhouse effect">greenhouse effect</a> with Revelle in the previous year, were early recruits to the faculty in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-Gribble_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gribble-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maria_Goeppert-Mayer" title="Maria Goeppert-Mayer">Maria Goeppert-Mayer</a>, later the second female <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureate</a> in physics, was appointed professor of physics in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-Gribble_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gribble-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The graduate division of the school opened in 1960 with twenty faculty in residence, with instruction offered in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Earth_science" title="Earth science">earth science</a>. Before the main campus completed construction, classes were held in the Scripps Institution of Oceanography.<sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman1_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>By 1963, new facilities on the mesa had been finished for the School of Science and Engineering, and new buildings were under construction for Social Sciences and Humanities. Ten additional faculty in those disciplines were hired, and the whole site was designated the First College, later renamed after <a href="/wiki/Roger_Revelle" title="Roger Revelle">Roger Revelle</a>, of the new campus. York resigned as chancellor that year and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/John_Semple_Galbraith" title="John Semple Galbraith">John Semple Galbraith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gribble_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gribble-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The undergraduate program accepted its first class of 181 freshman at <a href="/wiki/Revelle_College" title="Revelle College">Revelle College</a> in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman1_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Second College was founded in 1964, on the land deeded by the federal government, and named after environmentalist <a href="/wiki/John_Muir" title="John Muir">John Muir</a> two years later.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego_School_of_Medicine" title="University of California, San Diego School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a> also accepted its first students in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-Gribble_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gribble-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Revelle_College_1980.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/Revelle_College_1980.jpg/220px-Revelle_College_1980.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/Revelle_College_1980.jpg/330px-Revelle_College_1980.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/Revelle_College_1980.jpg/440px-Revelle_College_1980.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Revelle_College_1980.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Revelle College, 1980
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Political theorist <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Marcuse" title="Herbert Marcuse">Herbert Marcuse</a> joined the faculty in 1965. A champion of the <a href="/wiki/New_Left" title="New Left">New Left</a>, he reportedly was the first protestor to occupy the administration building in a demonstration organized by his student, political activist <a href="/wiki/Angela_Davis" title="Angela Davis">Angela Davis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Barberella_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barberella-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Legion" title="American Legion">American Legion</a> offered to buy out the remainder of Marcuse's contract for $20,000; the Regents censured Chancellor McGill for defending Marcuse on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Academic_freedom" title="Academic freedom">academic freedom</a>, but further action was averted after local leaders expressed support for Marcuse.<sup id="cite_ref-Gribble_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gribble-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Further student unrest was felt at the university, as the United States increased its involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> during the early 1960s, when a student raised a <a href="/wiki/Viet_Minh" title="Viet Minh">Viet Minh</a> flag over the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman1_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Protests escalated as the war continued and were only exacerbated after the National Guard <a href="/wiki/Kent_State_shootings" title="Kent State shootings">fired on student protesters</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kent_State_University" title="Kent State University">Kent State University</a> in 1970. Over 200 students occupied Urey Hall, with one student setting himself on fire in protest of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Stadtman1_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stadtman1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Early research activity and faculty quality, notably in the sciences, was integral to shaping the focus and culture of the university. Even before UC San Diego had its own campus, faculty recruits had already made significant research breakthroughs, such as the <a href="/wiki/Keeling_Curve" title="Keeling Curve">Keeling Curve</a>, a graph that plots rapidly increasing carbon dioxide levels in the atmosphere and was the first significant evidence for global <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Kohn%E2%80%93Sham_equations" title="Kohn?Sham equations">Kohn?Sham equations</a>, used to investigate particular atoms and molecules in <a href="/wiki/Quantum_chemistry" title="Quantum chemistry">quantum chemistry</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Miller-Urey_experiment" title="Miller-Urey experiment" class="mw-redirect">Miller-Urey experiment</a>, which gave birth to the field of <a href="/wiki/Prebiotic_chemistry" title="Prebiotic chemistry" class="mw-redirect">prebiotic chemistry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Engineering, particularly computer science, became an important part of the university's academics as it matured. University researchers helped develop <a href="/wiki/UCSD_Pascal" title="UCSD Pascal">UCSD Pascal</a>, an early machine-independent programming language that later heavily influenced <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation_Network" title="National Science Foundation Network">National Science Foundation Network</a>, a precursor to the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Network_News_Transfer_Protocol" title="Network News Transfer Protocol">Network News Transfer Protocol</a> during the late 1970s to 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In economics, the methods for analyzing economic <a href="/wiki/Time_series" title="Time series">time series</a> with time-varying <a href="/wiki/Volatility_(finance)" title="Volatility (finance)">volatility</a> (<a href="/wiki/Autoregressive_conditional_heteroskedasticity" title="Autoregressive conditional heteroskedasticity">ARCH</a>), and with common trends (<a href="/wiki/Cointegration" title="Cointegration">cointegration</a>) were developed. UCSD maintained its research intense character after its founding, racking up <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation#University_of_California.2C_San_Diego" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">20 Nobel Laureates</a> affiliated within 50 years of history; a rate of four per decade.</p> 
     <p>Under <a href="/wiki/Richard_C._Atkinson" title="Richard C. Atkinson">Richard C. Atkinson</a>'s leadership as chancellor from 1980 to 1995, the university strengthened its ties with the city of San Diego by encouraging <a href="/wiki/Technology_transfer" title="Technology transfer">technology transfer</a> with developing companies, transforming San Diego into a world leader in technology-based industries. He oversaw a rapid expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Jacobs_School_of_Engineering" title="Jacobs School of Engineering">School of Engineering</a>, later renamed after <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Irwin_M._Jacobs" title="Irwin M. Jacobs">Irwin M. Jacobs</a>, with the construction of the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Supercomputer_Center" title="San Diego Supercomputer Center">San Diego Supercomputer Center</a><sup id="cite_ref-Occupation_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Occupation-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> and establishment of the computer science, electrical engineering, and bioengineering departments.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Private donations increased from $15 million to nearly $50 million annually, faculty expanded by nearly 50%, and enrollment doubled to about 18,000 students during his administration. By the end of his chancellorship, the quality of UC San Diego graduate programs was ranked tenth in the nation by the National Research Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Raymond_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raymond-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university continued to undergo further expansion during the first decade of the new millennium with the establishment and construction of two new professional schools ?&nbsp;the <a href="/wiki/Skaggs_School_of_Pharmacy" title="Skaggs School of Pharmacy">Skaggs School of Pharmacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rady_School_of_Management" title="Rady School of Management">Rady School of Management</a>&nbsp;? and the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_for_Telecommunications_and_Information_Technology" title="California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology">California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology</a>, a research institute run jointly with <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine" title="University of California, Irvine">UC Irvine</a>. UC San Diego also reached two financial milestones during this time, becoming the first university in the western region to raise over $1 billion in its eight-year fundraising campaign in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-ucsdnews.ucsd.edu_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucsdnews.ucsd.edu-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> and also obtaining an additional $1 billion through research contracts and grants in a single fiscal year for the first time in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite this, due to the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9312_California_budget_crisis" title="2008?12 California budget crisis">California budget crisis</a>, the university loaned $40 million against its own assets in 2009 to offset a significant reduction in state educational appropriations.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The salary of <a href="/wiki/Pradeep_Khosla" title="Pradeep Khosla">Pradeep Khosla</a>, who became chancellor in 2012, has been the subject of controversy amidst continued budget cuts and tuition increases.<sup id="cite_ref-Chancellor_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chancellor-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1098px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Earl Warren College mall. From left to right: Geisel Library, Engineering Building Unit (EBU) I, the Powell-Focht Bioengineering Building, the Computer Science Building, and EBU II (visible through trees)"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg/1090px-UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg" width="1090" height="212" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg/1635px-UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg/2180px-UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg 2x" /></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCSD-Warren_Pano.jpg" title="Enlarge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         Panorama of 
         <a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren_College" title="Earl Warren College">Earl Warren College</a> mall. From left to right: 
         <a href="/wiki/Geisel_Library" title="Geisel Library">Geisel Library</a>, Engineering Building Unit (EBU) I, the Powell-Focht Bioengineering Building, the Computer Science Building, and EBU II (visible through trees)
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UC San Diego is located in the residential neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/La_Jolla" title="La Jolla">La Jolla</a> of northern <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, bordered by the communities of <a href="/wiki/La_Jolla_Shores" title="La Jolla Shores">La Jolla Shores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torrey_Pines,_San_Diego" title="Torrey Pines, San Diego">Torrey Pines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_City,_San_Diego" title="University City, San Diego">University City</a>. The main campus consists of 761 buildings that occupy 1,152 acres (466&nbsp;ha), with natural reserves covering about 889 acres (360&nbsp;ha) and outlying facilities taking up the remaining area.<sup id="cite_ref-Area_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Area-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5_in_California" title="Interstate 5 in California">San Diego Freeway</a> passes through the campus and separates the <a href="/wiki/UC_San_Diego_Health_System" title="UC San Diego Health System">UC San Diego Medical Center</a> and Mesa apartment housing from the greater part of the university. The <a href="/wiki/Preuss_School" title="Preuss School">Preuss School</a>, a college-preparatory <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">charter school</a> established and administered by UCSD, also lies on the eastern portion of the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Standing at the center of the university is the iconic <a href="/wiki/Geisel_Library" title="Geisel Library">Geisel Library</a>, named after <a href="/wiki/Dr._Seuss" title="Dr. Seuss">Dr. Seuss</a>. Library Walk, a heavily traveled pathway leading from the library to Gilman Drive, lies adjacent or close to <a href="/wiki/Price_Center" title="Price Center">Price Center</a>, Center Hall, International Center, and various student services buildings, including the Student Services Center and the Career Services building. The layout of the main campus centers around <a href="/wiki/Geisel_Library" title="Geisel Library">Geisel Library</a>, which is roughly surrounded by the six residential colleges of <a href="/wiki/Revelle_College" title="Revelle College">Revelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Muir_College" title="John Muir College">Muir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall_College" title="Thurgood Marshall College">Marshall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren_College" title="Earl Warren College">Warren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt_College" title="Eleanor Roosevelt College">Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sixth_College" title="Sixth College">Sixth</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego_School_of_Medicine" title="University of California, San Diego School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a>. The six colleges maintain separate housing facilities for their students and each college's buildings are differentiated by distinct architectural styles. As residential colleges were added while the university expanded, buildings in newer colleges were designed with styles that were starkly different from that of the original campus.</p> 
     <p>In addition to its academic and housing facilities, the campus features eucalyptus groves,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Birch_Aquarium" title="Birch Aquarium">Birch Aquarium</a> and museum, and several major research centers. The Scripps Institution owns a sea port and several open ocean vessels for marine research.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Several large shake facilities, including the world record holding Large High Performance Outdoor Shake Table, used for earthquake simulations, are also maintained by the university.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has actively sought to reduce carbon emissions and energy usage on campus, earning a ?gold? sustainability performance rating in the Sustainability Tracking Assessment and Rating System (STARS) survey. It was also praised in <i>The Princeton Review?s Guide to 322 Green Colleges: 2013 Edition</i> for its strong commitment to sustainability in its academic offerings, campus infrastructure, activities and career preparation.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_facilities">Academic facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Academic facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Center_Hall_Front,_UCSD.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Center_Hall_Front%2C_UCSD.JPG/220px-Center_Hall_Front%2C_UCSD.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Center_Hall_Front%2C_UCSD.JPG/330px-Center_Hall_Front%2C_UCSD.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Center_Hall_Front%2C_UCSD.JPG/440px-Center_Hall_Front%2C_UCSD.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Center_Hall_Front,_UCSD.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Center Hall, a lecture hall near the center of campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>When the campus opened in 1964, it consisted only of <a href="/wiki/Revelle_College" title="Revelle College">Revelle College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Institution_of_Oceanography" title="Scripps Institution of Oceanography">Scripps Institution of Oceanography</a>. The school's rapid increase in enrollment and opening to undergraduate students over its first decade spurred major campus expansion. <a href="/wiki/John_Muir_College" title="John Muir College">Muir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall_College" title="Thurgood Marshall College">Marshall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren_College" title="Earl Warren College">Warren</a> Colleges were established and built during the late 1960s through 1980s as the student population continued to grow considerably. Initially, the campus followed a rough north-south axis alongside <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_101_in_California" title="U.S. Route 101 in California">Historic Route 101</a>, though construction in the following decades deviated from this, with the core of the campus shifting towards Geisel Library.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since the merging of the school's two engineering departments into a single <a href="/wiki/Jacobs_School_of_Engineering" title="Jacobs School of Engineering">School of Engineering</a> in 1982, new buildings have been continually added as the division expands. Major additions include: the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Supercomputer_Center" title="San Diego Supercomputer Center">San Diego Supercomputer Center</a>, completed in 1986; the Powell-Focht Bioengineering Hall, completed in 2003; and the Structural and Materials Engineering building, completed in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Occupation_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Occupation-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Significant construction work on the previously undeveloped northern part of campus also took place during this time. Two graduate professional schools, the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_School_of_International_Relations_and_Pacific_Studies" title="Graduate School of International Relations and Pacific Studies">Graduate School of International Relations and Pacific Studies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rady_School_of_Management" title="Rady School of Management">Rady School of Management</a>, were constructed in the area adjacent to and near the Supercomputer Center, as well as <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt_College" title="Eleanor Roosevelt College">Roosevelt College</a>, a transfer student apartment complex called the Village, and <a href="/wiki/RIMAC_Arena" title="RIMAC Arena">RIMAC Arena</a>. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Prebys_Music_Center" title="Conrad Prebys Music Center">Conrad Prebys Music Center</a> was completed in 2009 as part of an expanding arts district to house UCSD's music department, renowned for its programs in experimental music.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_art">Public art</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Public art">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Collection" title="Stuart Collection">Stuart Collection</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sun_God_-_Front,_UCSD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Sun_God_-_Front%2C_UCSD.jpg/220px-Sun_God_-_Front%2C_UCSD.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Sun_God_-_Front%2C_UCSD.jpg/330px-Sun_God_-_Front%2C_UCSD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Sun_God_-_Front%2C_UCSD.jpg/440px-Sun_God_-_Front%2C_UCSD.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sun_God_-_Front,_UCSD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <i>Sun God</i>, part of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Collection" title="Stuart Collection">Stuart Collection</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>More than a dozen public art projects, part of the <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Collection" title="Stuart Collection">Stuart Collection</a>, decorate the campus. Perhaps the most famous of these is the <a href="/wiki/Sun_God_(statue)" title="Sun God (statue)">Sun God</a>, a large winged creature located near the Faculty Club. Other collection pieces include a collection of <a href="/wiki/Stonehenge" title="Stonehenge">Stonehenge</a>-like stone blocks, a house sitting atop an engineering building in Warren College called <i>Fallen Star</i>, a table by <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Holzer" title="Jenny Holzer">Jenny Holzer</a>, a building that flashes the names of vices and virtues in bright neon lights, and three metallic <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">Eucalyptus</a> trees.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Snake_Path,_UCSD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Image of the Snake Path taken from one of the upper floors in Geisel Library." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Snake_Path%2C_UCSD.jpg/220px-Snake_Path%2C_UCSD.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Snake_Path%2C_UCSD.jpg/330px-Snake_Path%2C_UCSD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Snake_Path%2C_UCSD.jpg/440px-Snake_Path%2C_UCSD.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Snake_Path,_UCSD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Snake Path, east of Geisel Library.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The collection also includes a large coiling snake path whose head guides towards Geisel Library, with a quote from <a href="/wiki/John_Milton" title="John Milton">John Milton</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Paradise_Lost" title="Paradise Lost">Paradise Lost</a></i> carved along its length: &quot;And wilt thou not be loath to leave this Paradise, but shalt possess a Paradise within thee, happier far.&quot; The path circles around its own garden and a large granite book-shaped block. One of the newest additions to the collection is Tim Hawkinson's giant teddy bear made of six boulders located in between the newly constructed <a href="/wiki/Calit2" title="Calit2" class="mw-redirect">Calit2</a> buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-Calit2_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calit2-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Another notable campus sight is the graffiti staircase of Mandeville Hall, a series of corridors that have been tagged with <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a> by generations of students over decades of use. Students in the university's visual arts department also create temporary public art installations as part of their coursework. The university is sponsoring a $56,000 <a href="/wiki/Performance_art" title="Performance art">performance art</a> project to develop a sense of community at the sprawling campus.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Graffiti_Staircase.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Graffiti_Staircase.jpg/220px-Graffiti_Staircase.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Graffiti_Staircase.jpg/330px-Graffiti_Staircase.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Graffiti_Staircase.jpg/440px-Graffiti_Staircase.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Graffiti_Staircase.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Graffitied staircase in Mandeville Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Shepard_Fairey" title="Shepard Fairey">Shepard Fairey</a>, most notable for his <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_%22Hope%22_poster" title="Barack Obama &quot;Hope&quot; poster">Barack Obama &quot;Hope&quot; poster</a>, painted a mural at the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A9_Caf%C3%A9" title="Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute;">Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute;</a>, one of UC San Diego most famous buildings and collectives, on an outside wall facing Scholars Drive, that features the likenesses of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> and other political figures. Underground street artist, Swampy, created a large piece inside the Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute;, visible through the courtyard depicting his signature mammoth skeleton. Local San Diego artist Mario Torero, in collaboration with university art students, painted a mural at the Caf&eacute; in commemoration of Angela Davis and Rigoberta Menchu, along with other notable political figures. The Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute; remains a hub for underground and politically progressive artists. Torero was invited back to the university in 2009 to create a mural called &quot;Chicano Legacy&quot; based on content suggested by <a href="/wiki/Chicano" title="Chicano">Chicano</a> students.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The mural is a $10,000 digital image on a 15-by-50-foot (4.6 by 15 m) canvas mounted on the exterior of Peterson Hall, which includes representations of <a href="/wiki/Cesar_Chavez" title="Cesar Chavez">Cesar Chavez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Huerta" title="Dolores Huerta">Dolores Huerta</a> as well as the kiosk structure at <a href="/wiki/Chicano_Park" title="Chicano Park">Chicano Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Berestein_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berestein-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UC San Diego maintains about 17,000 parking spaces and offers a number of alternative transportation options.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The university runs a shuttle system, which is provided free for students, faculty, and staff, that services the main campus, UC San Diego Medical Center, university affiliated research centers, and nearby apartment complexes and shopping centers. As part of a greater initiative to reduce the university's impact on the environment, a portion of the shuttle fleet has been refitted to exclusively use biodiesel fuel derived from vegetable oil.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSD also subsidizes public transit for commuters living near the campus, reserves parking spaces for carpools, maintains a fleet of on-campus <a href="/wiki/Zipcar" title="Zipcar">Zipcars</a>, and provides free bike rentals.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Association_of_Governments" title="San Diego Association of Governments">San Diego Association of Governments</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Metropolitan_Transit_System" title="San Diego Metropolitan Transit System">Metropolitan Transit System</a> are planning to bring <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Trolley" title="San Diego Trolley">San Diego Trolley</a> service to the local area. The project will extend the existing <b><a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(San_Diego_Trolley)" title="Blue Line (San Diego Trolley)"><span style="color:#0071bc;">Blue Line</span></a></b> north to UC San Diego and the University City area from Downtown San Diego. The extension will give the university campus two trolley stations, East and West. A major goal of the project is to ease traffic and parking on campus while providing more accessible transportation to nearby areas. There is also a proposed station at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Veterans_Affairs" title="United States Department of Veterans Affairs">Veterans Administration</a> hospital just south of UCSD. Construction is scheduled to start in 2014 and complete by 2017, with service beginning in 2018.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics_and_administration">Academics and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Academics and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Geisel_library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Geisel_library.jpg/220px-Geisel_library.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Geisel_library.jpg/330px-Geisel_library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Geisel_library.jpg/440px-Geisel_library.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Geisel_library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Geisel_Library" title="Geisel Library">Geisel Library</a>, named for Theodor Geisel, who was better known as 
        <a href="/wiki/Dr._Seuss" title="Dr. Seuss">Dr. Seuss</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UC San Diego is a large, primarily residential, public research university accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="Western Association of Schools and Colleges">Western Association of Schools and Colleges</a> that offers a four-year <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor of Science</a> degree to undergraduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The full-time undergraduate program comprises the majority of enrollments at the university. The university offers 125 bachelors degree programs organized into five disciplinary divisions: arts and humanities, biological sciences, engineering, mathematics and physical sciences, and social sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Students are also free to design special majors or engage in dual majors.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> 38% of undergraduates major in the social sciences, followed by 25% in biological sciences, 18% in engineering, 8% in sciences and math, 4% in humanities, and 3% in the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC San Diego's comprehensive graduate program is composed of several divisions and professional schools, including the <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Institution_of_Oceanography" title="Scripps Institution of Oceanography">Scripps Institution of Oceanography</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_California_at_San_Diego_School_of_Medicine" title="University of California at San Diego School of Medicine" class="mw-redirect">School of Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Engineering_in_Medicine" title="Institute of Engineering in Medicine" class="mw-redirect">Institute of Engineering in Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graduate_School_of_International_Relations_and_Pacific_Studies" title="Graduate School of International Relations and Pacific Studies">Graduate School of International Relations and Pacific Studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacobs_School_of_Engineering" title="Jacobs School of Engineering">Jacobs School of Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rady_School_of_Management" title="Rady School of Management">Rady School of Management</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Skaggs_School_of_Pharmacy" title="Skaggs School of Pharmacy">Skaggs School of Pharmacy</a>. The university offers 35 masters programs, 47 doctoral programs, 5 professional programs, and 9 joint doctoral programs with <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">San Diego State University</a> and other UC campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-Fast_Facts_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fast_Facts-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> UC San Diego has highly ranked graduate programs in biological sciences and medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_USNWR_Medc_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_USNWR_Medc-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> economics, social and behavioral sciences, physics, and computer engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also offers a continuing and public education program through the UC San Diego Extension.<sup id="cite_ref-extension_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extension-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Approximately 50,000 enrollees per year are educated in this branch of the university,<sup id="cite_ref-extension_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extension-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> which offers over 90 certificate and 12 specialized study programs.<sup id="cite_ref-extension_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extension-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Courses are offered at Extension facilities, located both on the main campus and off-campus, and also online.<sup id="cite_ref-extension_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extension-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_colleges">Residential colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Residential colleges">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UC San Diego's undergraduate division is organized into six <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential colleges</a>, each headed by its own <a href="/wiki/Provost_(education)" title="Provost (education)">provost</a>. They all set their own general education requirements, manage separate administrative and advising staff, grant unique degrees, and hold different commencement ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In chronological order by date of foundation, the six colleges are:</p> 
     <ol> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Revelle_College" title="Revelle College">Revelle College</a>, founded in 1964 as First College, emphasizes a &quot;Renaissance education&quot; through the Humanities sequence which integrates history, literature, and philosophy. It has highly structured requirements.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/John_Muir_College" title="John Muir College">John Muir College</a>, founded in 1967 as Second College, emphasizes a &quot;spirit of self-sufficiency and individual choice&quot; and offers loosely structured general-education requirements.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall_College" title="Thurgood Marshall College">Thurgood Marshall College</a>, founded in 1970 as Third College, emphasizes &quot;scholarship, social responsibility and the belief that a liberal arts education must include an understanding of one's role in society&quot;.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren_College" title="Earl Warren College">Earl Warren College</a>, founded in 1974 as Fourth College, requires students to pursue a major of their choice while also requiring two &quot;programs of concentration&quot; in disciplines unrelated to each other and to their major &quot;toward a life in balance&quot;.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt_College" title="Eleanor Roosevelt College">Eleanor Roosevelt College</a>, founded in 1988 as Fifth College, which focuses its core education program on a cross-cultural interdisciplinary course sequence entitled &quot;Making of the Modern World&quot;, has a foreign language requirement, and encourages studying abroad.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Sixth_College" title="Sixth College">Sixth College</a>, founded in 2002 with a focus on &quot;historical and philosophical connections among culture, art and technology.&quot;</li> 
     </ol> 
     <p>Students affiliate with a college based upon its particular philosophy and environment as majors are not exclusive to specific colleges. Muir and Warren enroll the largest number of undergraduate students, followed by Marshall, Revelle, Roosevelt, and Sixth.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Each undergraduate college sets different requirements for awarding graduation and provost's honors, separate from departmental and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa_Society" title="Phi Beta Kappa Society">Phi Beta Kappa</a> honors.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_admissions">Rankings and admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rankings and admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="infobox vcard" style="width: 22em">

     <p><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">Institutional rankings</a> of UC San Diego have generally ranked the university highly, depending on the criteria of the publication.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> For instance, the <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i> has ranked the university first in the nation since 2010 based on its contribution to the public good in three broad categories: social mobility (recruiting and graduating low-income students), research (producing cutting-edge scholarship and PhDs), and service (encouraging students to give something back to their country).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013, UC San Diego was ranked 38th among the top universities in the United States, tied for 3rd of the University of California schools, and 8th among public universities by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> ranked UCSD 10th out of the top 100 best-value public colleges and universities in the nation, and 3rd in California.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>ScienceWatch</i> ranks UCSD 7th of federally funded U.S. universities, based on the citation impact of their published research in major fields of science and the social sciences and 12th globally by volume of citations.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Internationally, the University of California, San Diego is ranked 14th by the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i>. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked UCSD 70th overall in the world, and 14th in life sciences and biomedicine.</p> 
     <p>UC San Diego ranked fifth in the nation in terms of federal research expenditure.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>ScienceWatch</i> placed UCSD 1st in <a href="/wiki/Social_psychology" title="Social psychology">social psychology</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> 2nd in <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">oceanography</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> 3rd in <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> 5th in <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> 17th in <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> and 18th in <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">Neuroscience</a> and <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">Behavior</a><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> using non-survey, quantitative based metrics to determine research impact. Research centers under university administration are: the <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Institution_of_Oceanography" title="Scripps Institution of Oceanography">Scripps Institution of Oceanography</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Supercomputer_Center" title="San Diego Supercomputer Center">San Diego Supercomputer Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_for_Telecommunications_and_Information_Technology" title="California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology">California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology</a>, and Center for US-Mexican Studies.<sup id="cite_ref-Calit2_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calit2-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table style="float:right; text-align:center; font-size:85%; margin:auto;" class="wikitable">

     <p>Admission to UC San Diego is highly selective;<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> for undergraduate admission in Fall 2013, it received over 82,000 applications from both freshman and transfer applicants, the third highest among the University of California campuses, and offered admission to 36.8% of those who applied.<sup id="cite_ref-recordfresh_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recordfresh-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Admitted students attained an average high school <a href="/wiki/Academic_grading_in_the_United_States#Grade_point_average" title="Academic grading in the United States">GPA</a> of 4.11 and an average combined SAT score of 1993 (average scores of 642 for critical reading, 692 for mathematics, and 659 for writing).<sup id="cite_ref-recordfresh_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recordfresh-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> 47% of admitted students receive federal <a href="/wiki/Pell_Grant" title="Pell Grant">Pell Grants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Graduate admissions are largely centralized through the Office of Graduate Studies. However, the <a href="/wiki/Rady_School_of_Management" title="Rady School of Management">Rady School of Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Institution_of_Oceanography" title="Scripps Institution of Oceanography">Scripps Institution of Oceanography</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_School_of_International_Relations_and_Pacific_Studies" title="Graduate School of International Relations and Pacific Studies">Graduate School of International Relations and Pacific Studies</a> (IR/PS) handle their own admissions. For Fall 2012, the UC San Diego School of Medicine offered admission to 5% of its applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2009, UCSD mistakenly sent Admit Day welcome emails to all its 47,000 freshmen applicants, instead of just the 17,000 who had been admitted.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> However, school officials quickly realized the mistake and sent an apology email within two hours.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a>
     </div> 
     <p>As one of the ten general campuses of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> system, UC San Diego is governed by a 26-member <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Board of Regents</a> consisting of 18 officials appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">Governor of California</a>, 7 <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_officio" title="Ex officio" class="mw-redirect">ex officio</a></i> members, and a single student regent. The current president of the University of California is <a href="/wiki/Mark_Yudof" title="Mark Yudof">Mark Yudof</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_(education)" title="Chancellor (education)">administrative head</a> of UC San Diego is <a href="/wiki/Pradeep_Khosla" title="Pradeep Khosla">Pradeep Khosla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Academic policies are set by the school's Academic Senate, a legislative body composed of all university faculty members.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Eight vice chancellors manage academic affairs, research, marine sciences, student affairs, planning, external relations, business affairs, and health sciences and report directly to the chancellor.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table style="text-align:center; float:right; font-size:85%; margin:auto;" class="wikitable"> 
      <caption>
       <i>Ethnic enrollment, Fall 2011<sup id="cite_ref-er_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-er-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></i>
      </caption>
