     </table> 
     <p>In 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> ranked UC San Diego as one of the &quot;happiest&quot; colleges in the United States, based on nightlife, number of student organizations, retention rate, and sunny days.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> In all, the university offers classical orchestras, <a href="/wiki/Intramural_sports" title="Intramural sports">intramural sports</a>, and over 550 student organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Thirty-eight national and local Greek organizations are hosted on campus,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> with fraternity and sorority members representing 20% of the student population.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The university operates on an <a href="/wiki/Academic_quarter_(year_division)" title="Academic quarter (year division)">academic quarter system</a>, with three primary quarters beginning in late September and ending in mid-June.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The undergraduate student body government is the UC San Diego Associated Students, organized as a cabinet and senate,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> while graduate students are represented by the Graduate Student Association, a proportional representative body with membership depending on the number of students in each graduate department.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, graduate students who serve as teaching assistants are represented by the UC-wide union of Academic Student Employees. Each of the six residential colleges has its own <a href="/wiki/Student_council" title="Student council">student council</a> as well. Most student media publications distributed on-campus are services provided and governed by ASUCSD, including Triton TV,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> a film studio and TV station, and the KSDT radio station.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> A notable exception is <i><a href="/wiki/UCSD_Guardian" title="UCSD Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, which is directly governed by the university's Student Affairs department.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Price_Center,_UCSD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Price_Center%2C_UCSD.jpg/220px-Price_Center%2C_UCSD.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Price_Center%2C_UCSD.jpg/330px-Price_Center%2C_UCSD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Price_Center%2C_UCSD.jpg/440px-Price_Center%2C_UCSD.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Price_Center,_UCSD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Price_Center" title="Price Center">Price Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Price_Center" title="Price Center">Price Center</a>, often referred to as PC, is the main student hub and is located in the center of campus, just south of <a href="/wiki/Geisel_Library" title="Geisel Library">Geisel Library</a>. The building houses multiple restaurants, the central bookstore, a movie theater, and office space for student organizations, organization advisers, and university faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> A student referendum was passed in 2003 to expand the Price Center to nearly double its original size. The <a href="/wiki/Price_Center" title="Price Center">Price Center</a> East expansion was officially opened to the public on May 19, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> There are also three campus centers that cultivate a sense of community among faculty, staff, and certain students: the <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">Cross-Cultural</a> Center, the <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">Women's Center</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> Resource Center. UC San Diego was the last UC campus to have such centers. All three, especially the Cross-Cultural Center that was created first, were founded in the mid-1990s as a result of student movements that demanded change despite opposition by the campus administration.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A9_Caf%C3%A9" title="Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute;">Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute;</a> is a student <a href="/wiki/Worker_cooperative" title="Worker cooperative">worker cooperative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_center" title="Social center">social center</a> that is perhaps best known for its role as a venue for underground music scene.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> It is an on-and-off again <a href="/wiki/Vegan" title="Vegan" class="mw-redirect">vegan</a> cafe and catering operation as well. The Ch&eacute; also acts as a resource for the music and art departments on campus through hosting art shows, performances, and film screenings. Some of the most notable touring bands or musicians who have played at the Ch&eacute; include: <a href="/wiki/Bon_Iver" title="Bon Iver">Bon Iver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rise_Against" title="Rise Against">Rise Against</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Eat_World" title="Jimmy Eat World">Jimmy Eat World</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_%26_Kim" title="Matt &amp; Kim">Matt &amp; Kim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Corgan" title="Billy Corgan">Billy Corgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blonde_Redhead" title="Blonde Redhead">Blonde Redhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Get_Up_Kids" title="The Get Up Kids">The Get Up Kids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deerhoof" title="Deerhoof">Deerhoof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bright_Eyes_(band)" title="Bright Eyes (band)">Bright Eyes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chumbawamba" title="Chumbawamba">Chumbawamba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Watt" title="Mike Watt">Mike Watt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hella_(band)" title="Hella (band)">Hella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Deacon" title="Dan Deacon">Dan Deacon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unwound" title="Unwound">Unwound</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jawbreaker_(band)" title="Jawbreaker (band)">Jawbreaker</a>. Prominent local San Diego bands such as <a href="/wiki/The_Locust" title="The Locust">The Locust</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pinback" title="Pinback">Pinback</a>, and national tours such as <a href="/wiki/Mates_of_State" title="Mates of State">Mates of State</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Dillinger_Escape_Plan" title="The Dillinger Escape Plan">The Dillinger Escape Plan</a> have given the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A9_Caf%C3%A9" title="Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute;">Ch&eacute; Caf&eacute;</a> some fame and praise as a radical vegan collective despite its small size and limited sound equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg/220px-Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg" width="220" height="458" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg/330px-Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg/440px-Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Watermelon_Drop_UCSD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The June 2007 Watermelon Drop, an annual tradition at 
        <a href="/wiki/Revelle_College" title="Revelle College">Revelle College</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The student body government coordinates a wide variety of concerts and events during the year. UC San Diego begins the fall quarter with Welcome Week to introduce new students to campus clubs and activities<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, ending the week with the All Campus Dance. Bear Garden, a carnival held near Price Center, takes place every quarter throughout the year. Additionally, events are frequently held at the Loft, a performance lounge within Price Center.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sun_God_Festival" title="Sun God Festival">Sun God Festival</a>, named after the <a href="/wiki/Sun_God_(statue)" title="Sun God (statue)">statue</a> part of the <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Collection" title="Stuart Collection">Stuart Collection</a>, is the largest and most significant event of the year, held annually in mid-May on the seventh week of the spring quarter<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The festival has grown over its thirty-year history into a 20,000 person event, featuring an eclectic mix of art, dance, and musical performances. Past performers have included: <a href="/wiki/Macklemore" title="Macklemore">Macklemore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silversun_Pickups" title="Silversun Pickups">Silversun Pickups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)" class="mw-redirect">Drake</a>, <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Third_Eye_Blind" title="Third Eye Blind">Third Eye Blind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Branch" title="Michelle Branch">Michelle Branch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sara_Bareilles" title="Sara Bareilles">Sara Bareilles</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a>, and <a href="/wiki/My_Chemical_Romance" title="My Chemical Romance">My Chemical Romance</a>. The 2013 festival will feature <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porter_Robinson" title="Porter Robinson">Porter Robinson</a>.</p> 
     <p>Two other popular campus traditions include the Pumpkin Drop and the Watermelon Drop, which take place during <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> and at the end of the spring <a href="/wiki/Academic_quarter_(year_division)" title="Academic quarter (year division)">quarter</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The Watermelon Drop is one of the campus' oldest traditions, famously originating in 1965 from a physics exam question centering on the velocity on impact of a dropped object. A group of intrigued students pursued that line of thought by dropping a watermelon from the top floor of Revelle's Urey Hall to measure the distance from the splat to the farthest travelling piece of fruit. A variety of events surround the Watermelon Drop, including a pageant where an occasional male but generally female &quot;Watermelon Queen&quot; is elected. The Pumpkin Drop is a similar event celebrated by the dropping of a large, candy-filled pumpkin from 11-story Tioga Hall, the tallest residential building on the Muir college campus.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The six undergraduate residential colleges have separate, unique housing facilities for their students. First-year students are usually housed in the residence halls while upperclassmen live in the college apartments. Transfer students are housed in separate facilities apart from the residential colleges, in an area adjacent to Eleanor Roosevelt College called The Village at Torrey Pines, which is most often called the Village.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The housing facilities vary in design, though nearly all of them are of <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modern</a> or <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">brutalist</a> style. The vast majority of entering freshmen and about forty percent of all undergraduates in Fall 2012 chose to live in campus residence halls or apartments,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> with roughly seventy percent of all incoming freshman living in triple occupancy rooms. Graduate students can choose to live in one of six apartment complexes apart from undergraduate housing.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Three of these facilities are several minutes away from UC San Diego while the remaining are located on university grounds.</p> 
     <p>Accommodations are made for students with specific needs. Undergraduate couples and families have the option of living in housing facilities that are normally available only to graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also dedicates a portion of its facilities for those who wish to live in <a href="/wiki/Gender-neutrality" title="Gender-neutrality" class="mw-redirect">gender-neutral</a> or LGBT housing.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Reflecting UC San Diego's diversity, International House, a complex of apartments located in Eleanor Roosevelt College, is dedicated to cross-cultural exchange between American and international students, housing about 350 students from more than thirty countries.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> International learning is fostered through formal programs including current affairs discussions, cultural nights, and a community newsletter. Upper-division undergraduates from all six colleges, graduate students, faculty, and researchers are eligible to live in International House, located in the Eleanor Roosevelt College townhouses. Demand is very high for this special program and there is often a waitlist. Spaces in International House are not guaranteed and admission requires a separate application.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Housing plans also offer students access to dining facilities, which were named by <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a> as the most <a href="/wiki/Vegan" title="Vegan" class="mw-redirect">vegan-friendly</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Each student is allotted a certain number of &quot;Dining Dollars&quot; to purchase meals at any dining hall and groceries at any on-campus market. Six distinct dining halls are located at each of the six colleges, with markets located adjacent or near them, except at Eleanor Roosevelt College which shares a marketplace with The Village. In addition to the six dining halls, there are also a number of specialty dining facilities on campus that accept dining dollars: Goodies, The Bistro and Club Med. UC San Diego currently offers four years guaranteed housing to its incoming freshmen, and two years to incoming transfer students.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ucsdtriton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/36/Ucsdtriton.jpg/220px-Ucsdtriton.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/36/Ucsdtriton.jpg/330px-Ucsdtriton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/36/Ucsdtriton.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ucsdtriton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Athletic mascot, the 
        <a href="/wiki/Triton_(mythology)" title="Triton (mythology)">Triton</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/UC_San_Diego_Tritons" title="UC San Diego Tritons">UC San Diego Tritons</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Most of UC San Diego's 23 intercollegiate varsity athletic teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_II_(NCAA)" title="Division II (NCAA)">Division II</a> twelve-member <a href="/wiki/California_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="California Collegiate Athletic Association">California Collegiate Athletic Association</a>, though some compete independently. Only the water polo, fencing, and men's volleyball teams compete as part of <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Before joining Division II in 2000, the school participated at the <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a> level.<sup id="cite_ref-Drooz_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drooz-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> In all, the Tritons have won a total of thirty national championships in golf, soccer, softball, tennis, volleyball, and water polo.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Until 2007, UC San Diego was the only Division II school that did not offer athletic <a href="/wiki/Scholarship" title="Scholarship">scholarships</a>. In 2005, the NCAA created a rule that made it mandatory for all D-II programs to award athletic grants. Consequently, a measure was proposed to begin offering $500 &quot;grants-in-aid&quot; to all 600 intercollegiate athletes in order to meet this requirement. A student <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> was passed in February 2007, authorizing a $329 annual student fee to fund a raise in coaches' salaries, hire more trainers, and provide all athletes with a $500 scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-Yang_Su_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yang_Su-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 2006-2007 season was marked as UCSD's best since moving to Division II, with nineteen athletic programs qualifying for post-season competition, including 17 for the NCAA Championships. Eight of those teams finished with a top five national ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The athletic department considered a move to Division I in 2011. The student body would have needed to approve a doubling of student fees to allow the university to meet minimum scholarship requirements for D-I participation. However, students overwhelmingly rejected this measure in 2012, halting any efforts for a move to Division I.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC San Diego does not have a football team. However, the university participated in intercollegiate football for one year during the 1968 season. The newly recruited Tritons lost all seven games that they played.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also offers 29 <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports club</a> teams, including <a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">badminton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">sailing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snow_skiing" title="Snow skiing" class="mw-redirect">snow skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">ultimate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Waterskiing" title="Waterskiing">waterskiing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Recreation_clubs_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Recreation_clubs-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The UCSD <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surf</a> team has won the national championship six times and is consistently rated one of the best surfing programs in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_San_Diego&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_California,_San_Diego_people" title="List of University of California, San Diego people">List of University of California, San Diego people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Over 150,000 <a href="/wiki/Alumni" title="Alumni" class="mw-redirect">alumni</a> are associated with UC San Diego.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable alumni include <a href="/wiki/Bill_Atkinson" title="Bill Atkinson">Bill Atkinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bud_Tribble" title="Bud Tribble">Bud Tribble</a>, members of the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Macintosh" title="Apple Macintosh" class="mw-redirect">Apple Macintosh</a> development team; biotechnology pioneers <a href="/wiki/David_Goeddel" title="David Goeddel">David Goeddel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Venter" title="Craig Venter">Craig Venter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Susumu_Tonegawa" title="Susumu Tonegawa">Susumu Tonegawa</a> (Physiology or Medicine), <a href="/wiki/Venki_Ramakrishnan" title="Venki Ramakrishnan" class="mw-redirect">Venki Ramakrishnan</a> (Chemistry) and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Beutler" title="Bruce Beutler">Bruce Beutler</a> (Physiology or Medicine). <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Mariano" title="Eleanor Mariano">Eleanor Mariano</a>, the first Filipino-American to reach the rank of <a href="/wiki/Rear_Admiral" title="Rear Admiral" class="mw-redirect">Rear Admiral</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> and first female director of the <a href="/wiki/White_House_Medical_Unit" title="White House Medical Unit">White House Medical Unit</a>, received her BS in Biology cum laude in 1977. A number of <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> authors including <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Benford" title="Gregory Benford">Gregory Benford</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Brin" title="David Brin">David Brin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Stanley_Robinson" title="Kim Stanley Robinson">Kim Stanley Robinson</a> earned PhDs at UCSD; cartoon animation producer <a href="/wiki/Mike_Judge" title="Mike Judge">Mike Judge</a> is also an alum.<sup id="cite_ref-Prominent_Alumni_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prominent_Alumni-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Buckley" title="Robert Buckley">Robert Buckley</a>, who stars as Clay on The CW television show <i><a href="/wiki/One_Tree_Hill_(TV_series)" title="One Tree Hill (TV series)">One Tree Hill</a></i>, graduated from UCSD with a degree in Economics. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kite_Runner" title="The Kite Runner">The Kite Runner</a>'</i>s <a href="/wiki/Khaled_Hosseini" title="Khaled Hosseini">Khaled Hosseini</a> is also a UCSD alumni as well as <a href="/wiki/Dileep_Rao" title="Dileep Rao">Dileep Rao</a>, one of the stars of the hit blockbuster movies <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i>. Rao spoke at the 2010 Convocation Dinner as he kicked off UCSD's 50th Anniversary Celebration. The three members of the popular Asian American filmmaking group <a href="/wiki/Wong_Fu_Productions" title="Wong Fu Productions">Wong Fu Productions</a>, Ted Fu, Phillip Wang, and Wesley Chan all graduated from UCSD as well. <a href="/wiki/Anna_Marie_Caballero" title="Anna Marie Caballero" class="mw-redirect">Anna Marie Caballero</a> is a former member of the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Assembly" title="California State Assembly">California State Assembly</a> and had previously served as the Mayor and Council member of <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_California" title="Salinas, California">Salinas, California</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chad_Butler" title="Chad Butler">Chad Butler</a>, drummer and co-founding member of the Grammy Award winning San Diego area based rock band <a href="/wiki/Switchfoot" title="Switchfoot">Switchfoot</a>.</p>
